At my age, 45, I’m standing here truly enjoying life I brought into this world. What else was so important at this stage that I would otherwise be spending my time on?

（04:31:00）我想从19岁起，我在《堡垒之夜》里已经累计玩了一千个小时，而且全都是和孩子们一起玩的。如果没有孩子们，我可能根本不会去玩《堡垒之夜》。嗯，也不能说绝对不玩，但要不是因为孩子，我肯定不会花一千个小时在《堡垒之夜》上。对我来说，乐趣在于能和他们一起做一件我自己也恰好喜欢的事情。我真的很喜欢《堡垒之夜》，这是一款非常出色的游戏。我不需要强迫自己陪他们玩。我经常主动问：“嘿，想不想一起玩《堡垒之夜》？”但即便如此，这也是一种我能与他们共享的活动，一种我能与他们分享的热情。最近我还开始和大儿子一起玩卡丁车。我自己开赛车已经很久了，现在他们也开始接触卡丁车。站在卡丁车赛道边，看着他们一圈圈地跑，看着他们越来越快，看着他们掌握这项技能，你不禁会想：除此之外，我的人生还能做什么更有意义的事呢？在我这个年纪——45岁，我站在这里，真正享受着自己带到这个世界上的生命。在这个人生阶段，还有什么事情比这更重要、更值得我投入时间的呢？

DHH
(04:32:00) … so important at this stage that I would otherwise be spending my time on.

DHH
（04:32:00）……在这个阶段，还有什么事情值得我去花时间做呢？

Racing

赛车

Lex Fridman
(04:32:04) All right. Like you mentioned, you like to race cars and you do it at a world-class competitive level, which is incredible. So how’d you get into it? What attracts you to racing? What do you love about it?

Lex Fridman
（04:32:04）好的。正如你提到的，你喜欢赛车，并且达到了世界级竞技水平，这真是令人难以置信。那么你是怎么开始接触赛车的？是什么吸引了你？你到底喜欢赛车的哪些方面？

DHH
(04:32:17) The funny thing about getting into racing is I did not get my driver’s license until I was 25. I grew up in Copenhagen, Denmark where the tax on cars is basically over 200%. So you pay for three cars and you get one, and I didn’t even have the money for one car, let alone three. So I could not afford a car growing up. We did not have a car growing up, but Copenhagen is a nice city to be able to get around on a bike or with a bus or as I did for a long period of time, on rollerblades.
(04:32:53) But when I was 25, I realized I wanted to spend more time in the U.S. I wasn’t sure yet that I was going to move there. That turned out later to be true, but I knew that if I wanted to spend time in the U.S., I needed to have a driver’s license. I was not going to get around very well if I didn’t know how to drive a car.
(04:33:10) So I got a driver’s license at 25. Then ended up moving to the U.S. later that year, and I’d always been into video games, racing video games. Metropolitan Street Racer on the Dreamcast was one of those games that really sucked me into … It was the precursor to Project Gotham, which was the precursor to essentially, Forza Horizon, I think.

DHH
（04:32:17）有趣的是，我直到25岁才拿到驾照。我在丹麦哥本哈根长大，那里的汽车税基本上超过200%。也就是说，你付三辆车的钱，才能买到一辆车。而我当时连一辆车都买不起，更别说三辆了。所以小时候我家根本负担不起汽车。我们成长过程中家里没有车，但哥本哈根是一座非常适合骑自行车、坐公交出行的城市——有很长一段时间，我甚至靠轮滑代步。
（04:32:53）但到了25岁那年，我意识到自己想在美国多待一段时间。当时还不确定是否要搬过去（后来确实搬了），但我知道，如果要去美国生活，就必须先拿到驾照。如果不会开车，在那里根本寸步难行。
（04:33:10）所以我25岁考了驾照，同年晚些时候就搬到了美国。我一直都很喜欢电子游戏，尤其是赛车类游戏。Dreamcast主机上的《Metropolitan Street Racer》就是一款让我深深着迷的游戏……我觉得它是《Project Gotham》的前身，而《Project Gotham》又可以说是《极限竞速：地平线》（Forza Horizon）系列的雏形。

Lex Fridman
(04:33:37) Oh, okay.
DHH
(04:33:37) I think that’s how the lineage goes. It’s just a great game. I actually just fired it up on an emulator a few weeks ago and it still sort of, kind of holds up because it has enough real car dynamics that it smells a little bit like driving a real car. It’s not just like an arcade racer like Sega Rally or something like that, but I’d always been into that.
(04:33:57) Then I got my driver’s license at 25 and moved to the U.S., and then two years later a friend that I’d met in Chicago took me to the Chicago Autobahn Country Club, which is this great track about 45 minutes from Chicago. And I sat in a race car and I drove a race car for the first time, and I had the same kind of pseudo-religious experience I did as when I started working on Ruby, where I did maybe 20 laps in this basically, a Mazda race car from, I think it was the ’90s or something, a pretty cheap race car, but a real race car. Single-seater, manual gearbox, but exposed slick wheels, all the stuff.

Lex Fridman
（04:33:37）哦，明白了。
DHH
（04:33:37）我认为游戏的发展脉络大致就是这样。那真是一款很棒的游戏。几周前我还在模拟器上重新玩了一下，发现它至今仍有可玩性，因为它具备足够真实的车辆动态，开起来有点像真的在驾驶汽车。它不像《世嘉拉力》（Sega Rally）那种纯粹的街机赛车游戏。我一直对这类拟真赛车游戏很着迷。
（04:33:57）后来我25岁拿到驾照并搬到美国，两年后，一位在芝加哥认识的朋友带我去了“芝加哥Autobahn乡村俱乐部”——那是距离芝加哥大约45分钟车程的一条很棒的赛道。我第一次坐进真正的赛车并驾驶它上赛道，那种体验几乎和我最初开始开发Ruby编程语言时一样，有种近乎宗教般的顿悟感。我记得当时大概开了20圈，驾驶的是一辆90年代左右的马自达赛车，虽然价格相当便宜，但确实是货真价实的赛车：单座、手动变速箱、裸露的光头胎，一应俱全。

(04:34:42) And after having had that experience, first of all it was just the most amazing thing ever. The physical sensation of driving a race car is really unique. And I think if you’ve driven a car fast, you have maybe a 2% taste of it. The exposure to the elements that you get in a single-seat race car, especially one like that where your head is actually out in the elements, you can see the individual wheels and sensation of speed is just so much higher, is at a completely different level.

（04:34:42）那次体验之后，首先让我觉得这是有史以来最震撼的事情。驾驶赛车带来的身体感受极其独特。如果你只是开过普通汽车高速行驶，那最多只能体会到其中2%的感觉。而在这种开放式座舱的单座赛车里——尤其是像那辆马自达那样，你的头部完全暴露在外——你能清楚看到每个车轮，速度感也因此被放大到一个完全不同的层次。

Lex Fridman
(04:35:13) So can you actually speak to that? So even in that Mazda, so you can feel … What, can you feel the track reverberating? You feel the grip?

Lex Fridman
（04:35:13）你能具体描述一下那种感觉吗？比如在那辆马自达里，你能感受到……什么？能感觉到赛道的震动吗？能感受到抓地力吗？

DHH
(04:35:22) Oh, yeah. Not only can you see the bumps because you’re literally looking straight at the wheels, you can feel all the bumps because you’re running a slick tire and it’s a really stiff setup. It’s nothing like taking a fast street car out on a racetrack and tried to driving a little bit around.

DHH
（04:35:22）哦，当然可以。你不仅能直接看到颠簸（因为你视线正对着车轮），还能真切感受到所有颠簸，因为使用的是光头胎，而且悬挂调校非常硬朗。这和开着一辆高性能街道车去赛道随便跑几圈完全是两回事。

Lex Fridman
(04:35:37) So can you feel the slipping, the traction?
DHH
(04:35:38) Yeah, you’d feel the slipping. That’s a huge part of the satisfaction of driving a race car, is driving in at the edge of adhesion as we call it, where the car’s actually sliding a little bit. A couple of percent of slip angle is the fastest way to drive a race car. You don’t want to slide it too much. That looks great, lots of smoke, but it’s not fast.
(04:35:58) How you want to drive it is just at the limit of adhesion where you’re rotating the car as much as your tires can manage and then slightly more than that. And playing at it, keeping it just at that level because when you’re at the level of, or at the limit of adhesion, you’re essentially just a tiny movement away from spinning out. I mean, it doesn’t take much. Then the car starts rotating. Once it starts rotating, you lose grip and you’re going for the wall.

Lex Fridman
（04:35:37）那你能感觉到打滑和抓地力的变化吗？
DHH
（04:35:38）是的，你能清晰感受到打滑。这正是驾驶赛车最令人满足的部分之一——我们称之为“在附着力极限边缘驾驶”，此时车辆其实已经在轻微滑动。大约百分之几的滑移角才是赛车最快的方式。你不能滑太多，虽然那样看起来很炫、烟雾缭绕，但并不快。
（04:35:58）理想的驾驶方式是刚好处于附着力的极限：让车辆旋转的程度达到轮胎所能承受的最大值，再稍微多一点点。你要不断微调，将车辆维持在这个临界点上。因为在附着力极限状态下，你离失控打转只差一个微小的动作。真的不需要多少失误，车子一旦开始旋转，就会立刻失去抓地力，直冲护墙而去。

(04:36:28) That balance of danger and skill is what’s so intoxicating, and it’s so much better than racing video games too because the criticality is taken up two notches. I often think about people who really like gambling, where I think, “Aren’t you just playing poker? No, the point is not poker. Poker is maybe part of it, but the point is that I could lose my house.” Right? That’s the addiction that some people get to gambling, that there’s something real on the line.
(04:36:58) When you’re in a race car, there’s something very real on the line. If you get it wrong, at the very least you’re going to spin out and probably hit a wall and it’s going to be expensive. At the very worst, you’re not getting out alive. And even if modern race cars have gotten way safer than they used to be, there is that element of danger that’s real, that there are people who still get seriously hurt or even killed in a race car.
(04:37:25) It’s mercifully rare compared to what it used to be when those maniacs in the ’60s would do Formula 1 and whatever, 13% of the grid wouldn’t make it to the end of the year because they’d just die in a fiery flaming fireball, but there’s still some of it there.

（04:36:28）这种危险与技巧之间的平衡令人无比陶醉，也远比赛车游戏刺激得多，因为其后果的严重性提升了好几个等级。我常常想到那些沉迷赌博的人：我会想，“你不是在打扑克吗？”但其实重点根本不是扑克。扑克或许只是载体，真正的吸引力在于“我可能会输掉整栋房子”。对吧？这就是某些人对赌博上瘾的原因——因为有真实的东西在赌注上。
（04:36:58）当你坐在赛车里，同样有非常真实的东西悬于一线。一旦出错，轻则失控打转、撞上护墙，造成昂贵损失；重则可能丧命。即使现代赛车已比过去安全许多，但危险依然真实存在——仍有人在赛车事故中受重伤甚至死亡。
（04:37:25）幸运的是，如今这类事故已比上世纪60年代罕见得多。那时的F1车手简直像疯子一样，每年约有13%的参赛车手因赛车起火爆炸而无法活到年底。尽管如此，危险的元素至今仍未完全消失。

(04:37:42) And I think that since that there’s something on the line really contributes to it, but it’s more than that. It’s not just a physical sensation. There’s activation of all your forces. There’s the flow, and I think that really cements why I got addicted, because I love that flow I got out of programming, but getting flow out of programming is a very inconsistent process.
(04:38:06) I can’t just sit down in front of a keyboard and go like, “All right, let’s get the flow going.” It doesn’t happen like that. The problem has to be just right. It has to meet my skills in just the right moment. It’s a bit of a lottery.
(04:38:19) In a race car, it’s not a lottery at all. You sit down in that car, you turn the ignition, you go out on track and I get flow virtually guaranteed because you need, or I need at least 100% of my brain processing power to be able to go at the speed I go without crashing. So there’s no time to think about dinner tonight or the meeting next week or product launch. It’s completely zen in actually, the literal sense of the word.
(04:38:49) I think of someone who’s really good at meditation, that’s probably kind of state they get into where it’s just clear you’re in the now, there’s nothing but you and the next corner. That’s a really addictive experience.
(04:39:02) So after I’ve had that, I couldn’t get enough. I kept going to the track every opportunity I got. Every single weekend for about four years, I would go to the track. And by the end of that time, I’d finally worked up enough skill and enough success with the company that I could afford to go “real racing.”

（04:37:42）我认为，正因为有真实的风险存在，才让赛车如此吸引人，但这还不是全部。它不仅仅是身体上的感受，而是调动了你所有的身心力量。那种“心流”状态，才是真正让我上瘾的原因。我很喜欢编程时进入的心流，但编程产生心流的过程极不稳定。
（04:38:06）我不能一坐到键盘前就说：“好了，现在进入心流吧。”事情不会这么简单。问题必须恰到好处，必须在我技能与挑战完美匹配的那个瞬间出现。这有点像抽彩票。
（04:38:19）但在赛车里，这绝不是彩票。你一坐进赛车，点火，驶上赛道，几乎就能确保进入心流状态——因为要以我那样的速度驾驶而不撞车，至少需要动用100%的大脑处理能力。你根本没有余力去想今晚吃什么、下周的会议或产品发布。这实际上就是字面意义上的“禅”（zen）。
（04:38:49）我想，那些真正擅长冥想的人，大概也会进入类似的状态：头脑清明，完全活在当下，除了你自己和下一个弯角，别无他物。这是一种极易上瘾的体验。
（04:39:02）自从有了那次体验后，我就再也停不下来。只要有机会，我就往赛道跑。连续大约四年，每个周末我都去赛道练习。到那段时间结束时，我终于积累了足够的驾驶技术，加上公司事业的成功，让我有能力去参加“真正的赛车比赛”。
(04:39:20) So I started doing that. I started driving these Porsches, and then as soon as I got into that, as soon as I got into “real competition,” I was like, “I wonder how far you can take this?” And it didn’t take that long before I decided, “You know what? I can take this all the way.”
（04:39:20）于是我开始这么做。我开始驾驶这些保时捷，而一旦我真正进入“正式比赛”，我就想：“我究竟能把这件事做到多远呢？”没过多久，我就下定决心：“你知道吗？我可以一路做到顶。”

(04:39:34) My great hero in racing is Tom Kristensen, fellow Dane. The Mr. Le Mans, as they call him, the greatest endurance race in the world. The 24 Hours of Le Mans has been won more times than any other by Tom Kristensen. He won the race nine times. So Tom just really turned me on to Le Mans. I’d been watching Le Mans since, I think, the ’80s. I have my earliest memories of watching that on TV. The race has been going since, I think, ’20s, but in the ’80s I got kind of into it.
（04:39:34）我在赛车界最崇拜的英雄是同为丹麦人的汤姆·克里斯滕森（Tom Kristensen）。人们称他为“勒芒先生”——这是世界上最伟大的耐力赛。汤姆·克里斯滕森赢得勒芒24小时耐力赛的次数比任何人都多，他赢了九次。正是汤姆让我真正迷上了勒芒。我想我从80年代就开始看勒芒比赛了，最早的记忆就是在电视上看这场比赛。这项赛事从20世纪20年代就开始举办了，但我在80年代才真正开始关注它。

(04:40:07) And then in the late ’90s, early 2000s when Tom started winning, I, like pretty much every other Dane started watching the race almost religiously. So I thought, “You know what? I want to get to Le Mans.”
（04:40:07）到了90年代末、21世纪初，当汤姆开始不断夺冠时，我和几乎所有其他丹麦人一样，几乎像履行宗教仪式般地观看这场比赛。于是我想：“你知道吗？我也想去勒芒。”

(04:40:18) This is the magic thing about racing, that if I get into basketball, I can’t set a realistic expectation that I’m going to play in the NBA, that I’m going to go to the finals, or I get into tennis and I’m going to play at Wimbledon. That just doesn’t happen. But racing is special in this way because it requires a fair amount of money to keep these cars running. It’s really expensive. It’s like having a small startup. You need to fly a bunch of people around the world and buy expensive equipment and so forth. So you need a bunch of capital, and I had some through the success of the company so I could do it, which meant that I could get to Le Mans.
（04:40:18）赛车神奇的地方就在这里：如果我去打篮球，我无法现实地期望自己能打进NBA、打进总决赛；如果我去打网球，也不可能指望自己能登上温布尔登赛场。这根本不可能实现。但赛车在这方面很特别，因为它需要相当多的资金来维持赛车运转——非常昂贵，就像经营一家小型初创公司。你需要让一群人飞遍全球，购买昂贵的设备等等。因此你需要大量资本，而我恰好通过公司的成功积累了一些资金，所以我能做到这一点，这意味着我真的可以去勒芒。

(04:40:50) So I set that as my goal. “I want to get to Le Mans,” and I started racing in real competition 2009, and three years later in 2012, I was at the grid of Le Mans for the first time.
（04:40:50）于是我设定了这个目标：“我要去勒芒。”我从2009年开始参加正式比赛，三年后的2012年，我第一次站上了勒芒的发车格。

Lex Fridman
(04:41:02) We should say, so Le Mans, 24-hour race, endurance. I mean, this is insane.
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:41:02）我们得说明一下，勒芒是一场24小时的耐力赛。我的意思是，这简直疯狂。

DHH
(04:41:10) There are three drivers, mind you. So it’s not like one guy just drives for 24 hours straight, but still it’s a pretty tough race, both physically and mentally, especially mentally. When you’ve been up for 24 plus hours, you’re not quite as sharp as when you first wake up.
DHH
（04:41:10）要提醒你的是，每辆车有三位车手。并不是一个人连续开24小时，但即便如此，这仍然是一场身心俱疲的比赛，尤其是精神上。当你已经连续清醒超过24小时，你的反应远不如刚醒来时那么敏锐。

(04:41:28) And this is funny about Le Mans too, it starts at around 4:00 in the afternoon, so you’ve already been up for half a day by the time the race starts and then there’s 24 hours to go before you’re done, and you’ll be in the car for anywhere from usually an hour and a half to a maximum of four hours. The regulations say four out of six is the max you can do.
（04:41:28）勒芒还有一个有趣的地方：比赛大约在下午4点开始，所以比赛一开始你就已经醒着半天了，然后还要再坚持24小时才能结束。你每次在车里驾驶的时间通常为一个半小时到最多四小时。规则规定，六小时内最多只能驾驶四小时。

(04:41:46) I’ve spent perhaps two and a half hours in a single stint at Le Mans. It’s pretty taxing. You’re going 200 miles an hour into some of these turns and there’s another 60 cars on track. Whenever I’m in my normal category, which is the LMP2 category, I have GT cars which are more like a Ferrari and a Porsche that I have to overtake, and then I have these hyper cars, which is the top-class that are overtaking me.
（04:41:46）我在勒芒单次最长驾驶过大约两个半小时。这非常消耗精力。有些弯道你以每小时200英里的速度冲进去，赛道上还有另外60辆车。当我处于自己常规的LMP2组别时，我需要超越那些类似法拉利和保时捷的GT赛车，同时还要被顶级组别的“超级跑车”（Hypercar）不断超车。

(04:42:14) So you got a lot going on and you got to stay sharp for two and a half hours straight to do that. That is just a guaranteed way to get incredible flow for long, long stretches of time. That’s why you get addicted to it. That was why I got addicted.
（04:42:14）所以你要处理大量信息，并且必须在整整两个半小时内保持高度专注。这绝对是一种能让你长时间进入“心流”状态的方式。这就是为什么你会对它上瘾——我就是因此上瘾的。

Lex Fridman
(04:42:27) You got to talk me through this video, this video of you in these LMP2s.
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:42:27）你得给我讲讲这段视频，就是你驾驶LMP2赛车的那段。

DHH
(04:42:31) Oh, yes.

莱克斯·弗里德曼

(04:42:34) Yeah, this was probably my favorite battle of my career.
DHH
（04:42:34）是啊，这可能是我职业生涯中最喜欢的一场缠斗。

Speaker 1
(04:42:41) And Heinemeier Hansson has beat past to add five-
旁白

DHH
(04:42:42) Yeah, so this is me driving against Nico Müller at the Shanghai International Circuit.
DHH
（04:42:42）对，这是我与尼科·穆勒（Nico Müller）在上海国际赛车场的对决。

Lex Fridman
(04:42:47) You’re on the outside here?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:42:47）你在这儿走的是外线？

DHH
(04:42:48) I’m on the outside in the blue and white and we go a whole track around with basically a piece of paper between us. See, down this back straight, I get so close to him because I want to force him over on the other side of the track such that he can’t just box me in, and we’ve been fighting already at this point for basically 40 minutes straight.
DHH
（04:42:48）对，我开着蓝白赛车在外侧，我们整整一圈几乎只隔着一张纸的距离。你看，在这条后直道上，我贴得非常近，目的是把他逼到赛道另一侧，这样他就没法把我夹住。到这个时候，我们已经连续缠斗了将近40分钟。

(04:43:06) I’ve been managing to keep this professional driver behind me for 40 minutes, and he finally passes me, but we just keep the battle on for the whole time. And it really just shows both these kinds of cars, the Le Mans Prototypes. We don’t actually ever touch. We get within about an inch and keep going around the Shanghai Circuit to-
（04:43:06）我一直设法让这位职业车手在我后面待了40分钟，他最终超过了我，但我们全程都在激烈缠斗。这也充分展现了勒芒原型车（Le Mans Prototypes）的特点：我们实际上从未发生碰撞，距离最近时只有大约一英寸，就这样绕着上海赛道一圈又一圈地较量——

Lex Fridman
(04:43:26) How did you get so good? I mean, that’s a fascinating story, right, that you are able to get so good?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:43:26）你是怎么变得这么厉害的？我的意思是，这真是个引人入胜的故事，对吧？你居然能达到这样的水平？

DHH
(04:43:34) I’m pretty good for the kind of driver I am, which is called the gentleman driver, which means I’m not a professional driver. And like many good gentlemen drivers, when we’re at our really best, we can be quite competitive with even professional drivers who have been doing this their whole life.
DHH
（04:43:34）以我这种“绅士车手”（gentleman driver）的身份来说，我已经相当不错了。“绅士车手”指的是非职业车手。和许多优秀的绅士车手一样，当我们发挥到极致时，甚至能和那些一辈子从事赛车的职业车手一较高下。

(04:43:50) The difference between us and the professionals is the professionals can do it every time, or more or less every time. So I can’t be this good all the time. When everything is just right, I can be competitive with professional drivers, but that’s not how you win championships. That’s not how you get paid by factories to drive. You got to be good every time you go out.
（04:43:50）我们和职业车手的区别在于，他们几乎每次都能稳定发挥出高水平。而我做不到每次都这么好。只有在一切条件都恰到好处时，我才能和职业车手竞争，但这并不是赢得冠军的方式，也不是厂队付钱请你开车的原因——你必须每次出场都表现出色。

(04:44:07) So that’s a huge difference. But some of it was also just, I really put my mind to it. By the time I realized race cars is what I want to do as my serious hobby, I put in thousands of hours.
（04:44:07）所以这是巨大的差距。但另一方面，我也确实全身心投入其中。当我意识到赛车是我真正想认真投入的爱好时，我已经投入了数千个小时的练习。

Lex Fridman
(04:44:21) Have you crashed? What’s the worst crash?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:44:21）你有没有撞过车？最严重的一次事故是什么样的？

DHH
(04:44:23) I’ve had a lot of crashes, but thankfully, knock on wood, I haven’t had any crashes where I’ve gotten really seriously hurt.
DHH
（04:44:23）我撞过很多次车，但谢天谢地，至今还没在事故中受过重伤。

Lex Fridman
(04:44:30) Have you wrecked the car?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:44:30）那你有没有把车撞毁过？

DHH
(04:44:31) Oh, yes. Oh, yes. I’ve wrecked many a cars.
DHH
（04:44:31）哦，当然有，当然有。我撞毁过很多辆车。

Lex Fridman
(04:44:34) So what’s that feel like, just you wreck a car? How do you get-
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:44:34）那撞毁一辆车是什么感觉？你怎么——

DHH
(04:44:37) It feels like total shit if you’re in a real race and other people depend on you. It’s not even so much the car, although it’s also sometimes that these cars are expensive to repair and that sucks and it feels so wasteful in a way when you crash some of these cars, but the sense that you’re letting a team down.
DHH
（04:44:37）如果你在正式比赛中撞车，而其他人又依赖着你，那种感觉糟透了。其实问题倒不完全在于车本身——尽管有时候修车确实非常昂贵，让人沮丧，而且撞毁这些车总让人觉得是一种浪费——但更糟糕的是那种辜负了整个团队的感觉。

(04:44:55) Endurance racing is a team sport. Not only do you have your mechanics, you usually have co- drivers. So when I crash, I just feel like, “Damn it, I could have avoided this.”
（04:44:55）耐力赛是一项团队运动。你不仅有机械师团队，通常还有队友车手。所以每次撞车，我都会想：“该死，我本可以避免这次事故的。”

Lex Fridman
(04:45:05) Yeah, but also you could have died.
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:45:05）是啊，但你也可能因此丧命。
DHH
(04:45:08) Do you know what’s funny? I never think about that. I don’t think you can because I think the moment you start thinking about being able to die, you can’t do it. You can’t go fast.

（04:45:08）你知道什么有趣吗？我从不去想那个。我觉得你根本不能去想，因为一旦你开始考虑自己可能会死，你就做不到了——你没法开得很快。

Lex Fridman
(04:45:18) Well, I’m sure, not to go all Carl Jung and Freud here, but I’m sure that’s always present in the back of your mind somewhere. You’re not just bringing it to the surface.

（04:45:18）嗯，我敢肯定——虽然不想在这里扯到荣格和弗洛伊德——但那种意识肯定一直潜藏在你脑海深处某个地方，只是你没有把它带到表层而已。

DHH
(04:45:31) It is in the sense that it’s part of the appeal. It’s part of the sense that there’s something on the line, that this isn’t just virtual. I can’t just hit reset, restart, reboot. If I crash this car, we’re going to be out, or we’re going to be disadvantaged, or it’s going to get destroyed, or I might get hurt.

（04:45:31）从某种意义上说，它确实是吸引力的一部分。这种感觉在于：有些东西是真正悬于一线的，这并非虚拟世界。我不能简单地按“重置”、“重启”或“重新启动”。如果我把这辆车撞毁了，我们可能就会退赛、处于劣势、车辆被毁，或者我自己会受伤。

(04:45:49) I’ve gotten lightly hurt a few times. I actually had, the year we won 24 Hours of Le Mans in our class, I’d been training in this Formula 3.5 car. It’s a really fast car, it’s a really nice exercise to do, but it’s also, it doesn’t have power steering. So some of these race cars, especially the open-seaters, they don’t have power steering, which means that the steering wheel is basically, directly connected to the front wheels.

（04:45:49）我曾受过几次轻伤。实际上，在我们赢得勒芒24小时耐力赛组别冠军的那一年，我一直在用一辆Formula 3.5赛车训练。那是一辆非常快的车，驾驶起来也很有意思，但它没有助力转向。有些赛车，尤其是开放式座舱赛车，是没有助力转向的，这意味着方向盘基本上直接连着前轮。

(04:46:19) So if you crash one of those cars and the front wheels suddenly turn, you’re really going to hurt your hands if you don’t get your hands off the wheel. I hadn’t raced enough of those cars to know that I had to get, or to have the instinct, to have developed the instinct that I had to get my hands off the wheel, so I didn’t and I really hurt my hand.

（04:46:19）所以如果你撞上这类车，而前轮突然转动，如果你不及时松开方向盘，手就会严重受伤。我当时还没开过足够多这类赛车，还不知道必须养成一种本能——在撞击时把手从方向盘上拿开。我没有这么做，结果手真的受了重伤。

(04:46:36) This was just, I think a month before the 24 Hours of Le Mans. So I thought, “Oh man, I’m going to have to miss it this year.” I had, not a cast. It was just seriously sprained. And then somehow, miraculously a week before the event, I was like, “Oh yeah, actually it’s okay now.” So, got to do it.

（04:46:36）那大概是在勒芒24小时赛前一个月左右。我当时心想：“天啊，今年我可能要错过比赛了。” 我的手没打石膏，只是严重扭伤。但神奇的是，比赛前一周，我突然觉得：“哦，其实现在好多了。” 于是我还是参赛了。

(04:46:51) And that would’ve been grave regret if I would’ve seen my team go on to win the race and I would have to sit on the sidelines. But I really have been quite fortunate in the sense that most of my crashes have just been expensive or sporting-inconvenient. They’ve never been something where I got seriously hurt, but I’ve seen plenty of people who have.

（04:46:51）如果我当时只能坐在场边，看着我的车队赢下比赛，那将会是巨大的遗憾。不过我真的相当幸运，因为我的大多数事故都只是代价高昂或对比赛造成不便，并没有让我受过重伤。但我见过太多人因此严重受伤。

(04:47:13) In fact, my co-driver this year, and for several years, Pietro Fittipaldi drove a race car at Spa. Spa is one of the great racetracks of all time and it has this iconic corner called Eau Rouge, which is probably the most famous corner in all of Motorsports that has a great compression before you climb uphill.

（04:47:13）事实上，我今年以及过去几年的队友皮耶特罗·菲蒂帕尔迪（Pietro Fittipaldi）曾在斯帕赛道（Spa）驾驶赛车。斯帕是史上最伟大的赛道之一，那里有一个标志性的弯角叫“Eau Rouge”，可能是整个赛车运动中最著名的弯角——在爬坡前有一段强烈的压缩区。

(04:47:34) It’s extremely fast, very difficult corner. And just as he does the compression, his car basically sets out and he loses his power steering and he drives straight into the wall and breaks both his legs and basically, face the prospect that maybe his career was over. I’ve had other teammates and people I know have serious injuries that’s really hurt them.

（04:47:34）这是一个极速且极难的弯角。就在他通过压缩区时，他的车突然失控，助力转向失灵，直接撞上了护墙，双腿骨折，几乎面临职业生涯终结的可能。我也见过其他队友和熟人遭受过严重伤害。

(04:47:57) And yet what’s funny, as you say, you’d think that would sink in. The year before we won in 2014, that same car had a Danish driver in it at Le Mans at the race I was driving, who died. He lost control of the car when there was a bit of rain on the track, and the track was unfortunately designed in such a poor way that there was a very big tree right behind the railing. And he hit that tree at full speed, pulled 90gs and was dead on the spot, which was just such an extremely awful experience to go through.

（04:47:57）但正如你所说，有趣的是，你会以为这种事会让人警醒。在我们2014年夺冠的前一年，那辆同一型号的赛车在勒芒比赛中由一位丹麦车手驾驶——那场比赛我也参加了——他不幸身亡。当时赛道上有点下雨，他失去了对车辆的控制，而赛道设计极其糟糕，护栏后面紧挨着一棵大树。他以全速撞上那棵树，承受了90个G的冲击力，当场死亡。那真是一次极其可怕的遭遇。

(04:48:42) I finished second that year, which should have been cause for a bunch of celebration, but it was just tainted by the fact that not only did a driver die, a fellow Dane died, a guy I knew died. That was pretty tough.

（04:48:42）那年我获得了第二名，本该值得庆祝，却因一名车手——一位同胞丹麦人，一个我认识的人——的去世而蒙上阴影。那真的很难受。

Lex Fridman
(04:49:01) So throw that into the pile of the things that have to be considered, is the weather conditions, like you mentioned of the track, whether it’s dry or wet.

（04:49:01）所以，把天气状况也算进必须考虑的因素里吧，就像你提到的赛道情况，是干地还是湿地。

DHH
(04:49:12) It’s a huge part of it. Even just last year at Le Mans, it was raining and I was out and I hadn’t made a serious mistake at 24 Hours of Le Mans since I did the first race in 2012, where I put it in the sand trap with four hours to go. And we lost a couple of laps getting pulled out, but it didn’t actually change anything for our result because that was just how the field was spread out.

（04:49:12）天气因素非常重要。就在去年勒芒，当时正在下雨，我出场了。自从2012年我第一次参加勒芒24小时赛以来，我一直没犯过严重错误——那次我在还剩四小时时冲进了沙石缓冲区，被拖出来耽误了几圈，但其实对最终成绩没太大影响，因为当时各车队之间的差距本来就很分散。

(04:49:41) I’d made minor mistakes over the years, but nothing that really set us out. And at the race last year when it was raining, I first clobbered a Ford Mustang when I made an overambitious pass on a damp part of the track and couldn’t stop in time and then felt absolutely awful as I sat in the gravel pit for two laps and knew that our race was over, a race where we were highly competitive.

（04:49:41）这些年来我犯过一些小错，但都没导致我们彻底出局。但在去年那场雨战中，我先是冒进地在一个湿滑路段超车，结果没能及时刹住，撞上了一辆福特野马（Ford Mustang）。随后我在碎石区里坐了整整两圈，心里难受极了，因为我知道我们的比赛已经结束了——那原本是我们极具竞争力的一场比赛。

(04:50:07) You’re not blessed with a competitive car, a competitive team and competitive setup every year. I know how rare that is. So to know that we had had a chance that year and I sort of squandered it felt really bad. But that got compounded when I got back on track, barely made it another stint and then put it into gravel trap again when it started raining on the entrance into Porsche.

（04:50:07）并不是每年都能拥有有竞争力的赛车、团队和调校。我知道这有多难得。所以意识到那年我们本有机会却被我浪费掉了，感觉真的很糟。更糟的是，当我重返赛道后，勉强跑完一段，又在进入保时捷弯（Porsche Curve）入口处开始下雨时，再次冲进了沙石缓冲区。

(04:50:29) So this is part of why racing is so addicting too because the highs are very, very high. When you win a race like the 24 Hours of Le Mans, it feels just incredible. There’s so much emotion, but if you fuck it up, the lows are very, very low.

（04:50:29）这也是赛车如此令人上瘾的原因之一：巅峰时刻极高。当你赢得像勒芒24小时这样的比赛时，那种感觉简直不可思议，充满强烈的情感；但如果你搞砸了，低谷也会极其低落。

Lex Fridman
(04:50:44) What are the things you’re paying attention to when you’re driving? What are the parameters? What are you loading in? Are you feeling the grip? Are you basically increasing the speed and seeing a constant feedback system effect it has on the grip, and you’re trying to manage that and trying to find that optimal slip angle?

（04:50:44）当你开车时，你关注哪些方面？有哪些参数？你在大脑中加载了什么信息？你在感受抓地力吗？你是不是在不断提速，观察抓地力反馈系统的变化，并试图管理它、找到最佳的滑移角？

(04:51:09) Are you looking around using your eyes? Are you smelling things? Are you listening, just feeling the wind or are you looking at the field, too? How’d you not hit that guy at all? You get close within inches, right? So you have to pay attention to that, too.

（04:51:09）你会用眼睛环顾四周吗？你会闻气味吗？你会听声音、感受风，还是会同时观察场上其他车辆？你是怎么做到完全不撞到旁边那辆车的？你们之间只差几英寸，对吧？所以你也必须注意这一点。

DHH
(04:51:26) It’s really interesting about that specific battle where we’re literally a few inches apart. I can’t fully explain it, but humans can develop an incredible sense of space where I can’t see the edge of the back of my car, but I can know exactly where it is. I can have a mental model in my head that gives me the exact dimensions of this car such that I can run within a few inches of a competitor car or within a few inches of the wall and not hit either when things go well.

（04:51:26）关于那种彼此仅隔几英寸的缠斗，其实非常有趣。我无法完全解释清楚，但人类可以培养出一种惊人的空间感：即使我看不到自己车尾边缘的位置，我也能精确知道它在哪里。我脑中会构建一个心理模型，准确掌握这辆车的尺寸，从而能在距离对手车辆或墙壁仅几英寸的情况下高速行驶而不发生碰撞——只要一切顺利。

(04:51:57) The car is about two meters wide and it’s quite long, five meters and you can’t see everything. The mirrors are actually kind of shit. There’s no rear-view mirror in these cars. You can’t see out the back. You can only see through your two side mirrors, but you form this intuitive mental model when you get good enough at this.

（04:51:57）这辆车宽约两米，长度接近五米，你不可能看到所有地方。后视镜其实很差劲——这些赛车根本没有车内后视镜，你看不到车后方，只能依靠两侧的外后视镜。但当你练到足够熟练时，就会形成这种直觉性的心理模型。

(04:52:14) But what I actually pay attention to most is I run a program. What I try to do when I go to a racetrack is I try to load up the best program I know how for every single corner. What’s my brake point? What’s my acceleration point? What’s my brake trailing curve? And I try to pick up that program in part just by finding it myself and how fast I can go. But even more so than that by copying my professional competitors, or not competitors, co-drivers.

（04:52:14）但我真正最关注的是运行一套“程序”。每次上赛道时，我会为每个弯角加载我能想到的最佳操作程序：我的刹车点在哪？油门点在哪？刹车释放曲线如何？我会部分靠自己摸索、测试极限速度来建立这套程序，但更多时候是通过模仿我的职业队友（不是对手，而是同队车手）来学习。

(04:52:45) So I usually always race with a pro, and modern race cars produce an absolute enormous amount of data, and you can analyze all that data after each outing. You can see an exact trace of how much you pushed the brake pedal, how much you did in terms of steering inputs, when you got on the gas. You can see every millisecond you’re losing is evident in those charts.

（04:52:45）所以我通常都会和职业车手搭档参赛。现代赛车会产生海量数据，每次出场后你都可以分析这些数据：你能看到自己踩了多少刹车、打了多少方向、何时踩下油门。图表上清晰显示出你每一毫秒的损失。

(04:53:09) So what I try to do is I try to look at the chart and then I try to load that in, and that’s what I got to do. “Oh, in this corner 17, I have to be 10 bar lighter on the brake,” so I try to load that program in and then I try to repeat it.

（04:53:09）所以我努力去看这些图表，然后把优化后的操作“加载”进自己的驾驶习惯中。“哦，在17号弯，我得把刹车力度减轻10巴。”于是我就把这个程序加载进去，然后反复执行。

(04:53:23) Now, then there are all the things that changes. Your tires change quite a lot. These tires are made to only last 40 minutes in many cases. Sometimes at Le Mans we can go longer, but at some racetracks they’ll last as little as 40 minutes before they really fall off. So you got to manage that, that the grip is constantly changing, so your program have to suddenly fit those changing circumstances.

（04:53:23）当然，还有很多变量会不断变化。轮胎状态变化尤其大。很多情况下，这些轮胎设计寿命只有40分钟。有时在勒芒我们可以用得更久，但在某些赛道，它们可能撑不到40分钟性能就会急剧下降。因此你必须管理好这一点——抓地力始终在变，你的“程序”也必须迅速适应这些变化。

(04:53:45) And then in endurance racing, you’re constantly interacting with other cars because you’re passing slower classes or you’re getting passed by a faster class. So that’s part of the equation. And then you’re trying to dance the car around the limit of adhesion.

（04:53:45）此外，在耐力赛中，你总在与其他车辆互动——你要超越慢速组别的车，也可能被更快组别的车超越。这也是驾驶策略的一部分。与此同时，你还在极限附着力边缘“跳舞”，让赛车保持在失控与可控之间的微妙平衡。
(04:53:59) So you got all those factors playing at the same time. But above all else for me is to try to become a robot. How can I repeat this set of steps exactly as I’m supposed to for two and a half hours straight without making 100 milliseconds worth of mistakes?
（04:53:59）所以所有这些因素都在同时发挥作用。但对我来说，最重要的是努力变成一台机器人——我如何能在整整两个半小时内，精确无误地重复这套操作步骤，连100毫秒的失误都不犯？

Lex Fridman
(04:54:17) Yeah. Low latency algorithm.
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:54:17）是啊，低延迟算法。

DHH
(04:54:20) That’s really a huge part of it actually. Your latency is enormously important in terms of being able to catch when the car starts slipping. You get this sensation in your body that the G-forces are a little off, the slip angle is a little off and then you have to counter steer.
DHH
（04:54:20）这其实真的占据了很大一部分。你的反应延迟极其关键，因为它决定了你能否及时察觉车辆开始打滑。你会在身体上感受到一种异常：G力有点不对劲，滑移角也略有偏差，这时你就必须反打方向。

(04:54:38) And obviously, the best race car drivers just feel like an intuition. I have some intuition. I don’t have all of it, so I do occasionally spin my car, but that’s the challenge.
（04:54:38）显然，最顶尖的赛车手几乎全凭直觉。我有一些直觉，但不是全部都有，所以我偶尔还是会把车甩出去，但这也正是挑战所在。

Lex Fridman
(04:54:48) From everything you’ve studied and understand, what does it take to achieve mastery in racing? What does it take to become the best race car driver in the world?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:54:48）根据你所研究和理解的一切，要达到赛车领域的精通需要什么？要成为世界最佳赛车手又需要什么？

DHH
(04:54:58) Obsession is part of it. When I read and hear about Senna and the other greats, they were just singularly focused. Max Verstappen is the current champion of the world and he is the same kind. Max has been fascinating to watch. I mean, he’s a phenomenal race car driver, but he also literally does nothing else. When he’s not at the racetrack, he’s driving sim racing. He’s literally in video games doing more racing when he’s not doing all the racing he’s already doing.
DHH
（04:54:58）痴迷是其中的一部分。当我读到或听到关于塞纳和其他伟大车手的故事时，他们都是极度专注的。马克斯·维斯塔潘是当今的世界冠军，他也属于这一类。看他比赛非常吸引人——他不仅是一位非凡的赛车手，而且几乎不做其他任何事。当他不在赛道上时，他就在玩模拟赛车；即便已经完成了大量真实赛车训练，他还会在电子游戏中继续练车。

Lex Fridman
(04:55:30) Is there a specific skill they have that stands out to you as supernatural through all of that obsession? Is it a bunch of factors or are they actually able to, like you said, develop a sense? Is it, they’re able to get to the very edge of the slip?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:55:30）在如此痴迷的背后，是否有一种特定技能让你觉得近乎超自然？这是多种因素的综合作用，还是说他们真如你所说，能培养出某种“感觉”？比如，他们能够精准地触及轮胎打滑的极限？

DHH
(04:55:45) They’re able to develop very fine-tuned sensibilities for when the car is sliding. They can feel just these tiny moments or movements in the chassis that transports up usually through their ass. That’s why you call it a butt meter that goes up and you feel like the car is loose, or you feel like you’re just about to lock up. You can really hone that tuning.
DHH
（04:55:45）他们能培养出对车辆滑动极其敏锐的感知力。他们能察觉到底盘中那些极其细微的瞬间或动作，而这种感觉通常通过臀部传递上来。这就是为什么人们称之为“屁股传感器”——你能感觉到车子开始松动，或者即将抱死。这种感知是可以不断打磨精进的。

(04:56:10) Then the other thing is you have to have really good reaction time. And when you look at great Formula 1 drivers, they can generally have a reaction time of just under 200 milliseconds, which is awesome, and even 10 milliseconds’ difference makes a huge difference.
（04:56:10）另一点是你必须拥有极快的反应速度。当你观察顶级F1车手时，他们的反应时间通常略低于200毫秒，这已经非常惊人了，而即便是10毫秒的差距也会带来巨大影响。

(04:56:26) You’ll see it when the Formula 1 grid, for example, they do a standing start and you see the five red lights come on. And when the last light goes out, they’re supposed to release the clutch and get going, and they can time this. So you can see exactly who has the reaction time.
（04:56:26）举个例子，在F1发车格上进行静止起步时，你会看到五盏红灯亮起。当最后一盏灯熄灭时，车手应立即松开离合器出发，而他们能精准把握这个时机。因此，你可以清楚看出谁的反应更快。

(04:56:40) And even being off by 20 milliseconds can make the difference of whether you’re in front or behind at the first corner.
（04:56:40）哪怕慢了20毫秒，就可能决定你在第一个弯角是领先还是落后。

Lex Fridman
(04:56:48) How much of winning is also just the strategy of jostling for position?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:56:48）胜利在多大程度上也取决于争夺位置的策略？

DHH
(04:56:53) There’s some of that, and some of it is also just nerve. Who wants it more? That’s exactly when that sense of danger comes in. There’s a great quote from Fernando Alonso when he was driving at Suzuka against Schumacher, I think.
DHH
（04:56:53）这方面确实存在，但有时候也纯粹是胆量的问题——谁更渴望胜利？这正是危险感介入的时刻。我记得费尔南多·阿隆索在铃鹿赛道与舒马赫对决时说过一句名言。

(04:57:09) They’re coming up to this incredibly fast corner. It’s very dangerous, and Alonso basically accounts, “I was going to make the pass because I knew he had a wife and kids at home.”
（04:57:09）当时他们正接近一个极高速的弯角，非常危险。阿隆索大致是这么说的：“我打算完成那次超车，因为我知道他家里有妻子和孩子。”

Lex Fridman
(04:57:22) That’s so gangster.
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:57:22）这也太狠了。

DHH
(04:57:23) Just absolutely ruthless, right?
DHH
（04:57:23）简直冷酷无情，对吧？

Lex Fridman
(04:57:25) Yeah. Wow.
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:57:25）是啊，哇。

DHH
(04:57:26) That, “I knew he valued life more than I did.” So there’s a bit of poker sometimes in that, who’s going to yield? There’s a bit of chicken raised in that regard, and sometimes it doesn’t work. No one yields and you both crash, but very often one person will blink first.
DHH
（04:57:26）“我知道他比我更珍惜生命。”所以这有时就像一场扑克博弈——看谁先退让。这就有点像“胆小鬼游戏”，有时双方都不退，结果双双撞毁；但更多时候，总有一方会先眨眼认输。

Lex Fridman
(04:57:41) Can the pass be both on the inside and the outside or is it-
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:57:41）超车可以在内线和外线都进行吗，还是说……

DHH
(04:57:44) You can pass wherever you want as long as you have just a slight part of the car on the racetrack.
DHH
（04:57:44）只要你的车还有一小部分在赛道上，你就可以在任何地方超车。

Lex Fridman
(04:57:50) And then you just improvise and take risks. What a sport. And then Senna, of course is a legendary risk-taker.
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:57:50）然后你就即兴发挥、冒险一搏。真是项了不起的运动。当然，塞纳就是一位传奇的风险承担者。

DHH
(04:58:00) Yes. And even before him. By the time … I mean, he died in the ’90s, but by the time we got to the ’90s, racing was already a lot safer than it was when Nik Lauda raced in the ’60s. That level of danger is no longer there. There’s still just a remnant of it and it is still dangerous, but nothing like that.
DHH
（04:58:00）是的，甚至在他之前更是如此。我是说，他是在90年代去世的，但到了90年代，赛车运动已经比尼基·劳达在60年代参赛时安全多了。那种级别的危险已不复存在，如今只剩一点残余，虽然仍具危险性，但远不及当年。

(04:58:21) And it’s a little hard to compare through the ages who’s the greatest driver of all time. I think there’s a fair argument that Senna is, but we don’t have the data. We don’t know who he was up against. How would he fare if we pitted him against Max Verstappen today?
（04:58:21）要跨时代比较谁是有史以来最伟大的车手，其实有点困难。我认为塞纳确实有充分理由被视为最伟大，但我们缺乏足够的数据。我们不清楚他当年面对的对手究竟有多强。如果今天让他和马克斯·维斯塔潘同场竞技，结果会如何？

(04:58:35) I do think sometimes that you can have a bit of a nostalgia for the all-time greats, but the world moves forward and new records are being set all the time and the professionalism keeps improving, sometimes to the detriment of the sport, I think.
（04:58:35）我觉得有时候人们对历史上的伟大车手怀有一种怀旧情绪，但世界在前进，新纪录不断被刷新，职业化水平也在持续提升——尽管我认为，这种提升有时反而损害了这项运动的魅力。

(04:58:48) There’s a lot of professional drivers who are not only just very good at driving, but are very good at being corporate spokespeople, and it used to be quite different. There used to be more characters in racing that had a bit more personality that they were allowed to shine because there weren’t a billion sponsorships on the line that they were afraid to lose.
（04:58:48）如今许多职业车手不仅驾驶技术高超，还非常擅长担任企业代言人，这和过去大不相同。以前的赛车界有更多个性鲜明的人物，他们可以展现自我，因为那时没有动辄数十亿美元的赞助合同让他们战战兢兢、不敢越雷池一步。

Cars

汽车

Lex Fridman
(04:59:06) Ridiculous question, what’s the greatest car ever made, or maybe what’s the funnest one to drive?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:59:06）问个有点荒谬的问题：有史以来最伟大的汽车是什么？或者，哪款车开起来最有乐趣？

DHH
(04:59:11) The greatest car for me of all time is the Pagani Zonda.
DHH
（04:59:11）对我来说，有史以来最伟大的汽车是帕加尼Zonda。

Lex Fridman
(04:59:15) Okay, I’m looking this up, Pagani Zonda.
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:59:15）好的，我正在查一下帕加尼Zonda。

DHH
(04:59:18) So the Pagani Zonda was made by this wonderful Argentinian called Horacio Pagani.
DHH
（04:59:18）帕加尼Zonda是由一位杰出的阿根廷人——奥拉西奥·帕加尼打造的。
Lex Fridman
(04:59:25) My God, that’s a beautiful car. Wow.
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（04:59:25）天哪，那真是一辆漂亮的车。哇。

DHH
(04:59:26) It’s a gorgeous car. You can look up mine. It’s the Pagani Zonda HH. Yep. So, that’s a car I had made in 2010 after we visited the factory in Modena, and by sheer accident ended up with this car, but it became my favorite car in the world basically. When I watched an episode of Top Gear, I think in 2005, where one of the presenters was driving the Pagani Zonda F around and I just thought, “That’s the most beautiful car in the world. It is the most incredibly sounding car in the world. If I one day have the option, this is what I want.”
DHH
（04:59:26）这辆车美极了。你可以查一下我的那辆——是帕加尼 Zonda HH。没错。这辆车是我在2010年参观完摩德纳的工厂后定制的，纯属偶然得到了它，但基本上它成了我这辈子最爱的车。我记得大约在2005年看过一集《Top Gear》，其中一位主持人开着帕加尼 Zonda F 转圈，我当时就想：“这绝对是全世界最美的车，也是全世界声音最震撼的车。如果有一天我有机会，我就要这一辆。”

(05:00:14) And then I had the option in 2010. I’ve had the car ever since. I’m never ever going to sell it. It’s truly a masterpiece that’s stood the test of time. There’s some great cars from history that are recognized as being great in their time. This car is still great.
（05:00:14）后来2010年我真的有了这个机会。从那以后我一直拥有这辆车，而且永远不会卖掉它。它是一件真正经得起时间考验的杰作。历史上有些伟大的车，在它们那个时代被公认为杰作，但这辆车至今依然出色。

Lex Fridman
(05:00:30) Have you taken it on the racetrack?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（05:00:30）你带它上过赛道吗？

DHH
(05:00:32) I have. It’s terrible at that. But I don’t want to say it’s terrible at that. That’s not what it’s designed for. It’s designed for the road and that’s why it’s great. There are a lot of fast cars that are straddling their race car for the road. You don’t actually want a race car for the world. A race car for the world is a pain in the ass. It’s way too stiff. It’s way too loud. It’s way too uncomfortable. You can’t actually take it on a road trip.
DHH
（05:00:32）我试过。它在赛道上表现很差。不过我不想说它“差”，因为它本来就不是为赛道设计的。它是为了公路而生，这才是它卓越的原因。现在有很多快车试图兼顾赛道和公路性能，但你其实并不想要一辆“能上路的赛车”。那种车简直让人头疼：太硬、太吵、太不舒服，根本没法用来长途旅行。

Lex Fridman
(05:00:55) So this actually feels good driving on normal roads?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（05:00:55）所以它在普通道路上开起来其实很舒服？

DHH
(05:00:55) Oh, totally, totally.
DHH
（05:00:55）哦，绝对、绝对舒服。

Lex Fridman
(05:00:59) And you, of course always go to speed limit?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（05:00:59）而且你当然总是遵守限速，对吧？

DHH
(05:01:00) Always. This is why I love having this car in Spain because they’re a little more relaxed. Not entirely relaxed, but more relaxed than they are in a lot of places. In Denmark, I kid you not, if you are on the highway and you go more than twice the speed limit, they confiscate your car and keep it. You’re not getting it back. They don’t even care if it’s your car or not. If you were borrowing my car and you went twice the speed limit, it’s gone.
DHH
（05:01:00）一直都是。这也是我喜欢把这辆车放在西班牙的原因——那里对超速稍微宽松一些。虽然不是完全放任，但比很多地方都宽松。在丹麦，我说真的，如果你在高速公路上超速超过限速两倍，他们会直接没收你的车，而且不会还给你。他们根本不在乎车是不是你的。哪怕你只是借了我的车，只要超速两倍以上，车就没了。

(05:01:26) So they don’t do that in Spain. I mean, in most places, except for the German Autobahn, they get pissy if you go twice the speed limit for all sorts of fair reasons. I’m not advocating that you should be going much more than that, but there are certain special roads where you can’t open things up and no one’s in harm’s way, and that’s an incredible sensation. And I do think that some of those speed limits actually are kind of silly, and I’m not just saying that in a vacuum.
（05:01:26）所以在西班牙他们不会这么做。大多数地方（除了德国的不限速高速公路）都会因为各种合理原因对你超速两倍的行为非常不满。我并不是鼓吹大家应该超速太多，但在某些特定路段，当你能尽情加速又不会危及他人安全时，那种感觉真是无与伦比。而且我认为，有些限速规定确实有点荒谬——我这么说可不是空口无凭。

(05:01:50) In Germany, they have the glorious Autobahn, and on the Autobahn there is no speed limit in a bunch of segments. And they’re so committed to their speed-limitless Autobahn, which is by the way, very weird of Germans. They usually love rules. They’re usually very precise about it, and then they have this glorious thing called the Autobahn.
（05:01:50）在德国，他们有著名的不限速高速公路（Autobahn），其中很多路段根本没有速度限制。德国人对这种不限速的 Autobahn 如此执着，其实挺奇怪的——毕竟德国人通常热爱规则，做事极其严谨，却偏偏保留了这么一条自由奔放的高速公路。

(05:02:09) There was a great case a couple of years ago where a guy took out a Bugatti Chiron, went 400 kilometers an hour on the Autobahn, and he filmed it and put it on YouTube and a case was brought against him because even though they don’t have a speed limit, they do have rules that you can’t drive recklessly, and he won the case. He wasn’t driving recklessly. He was just going very, very fast.
（05:02:09）几年前有个著名案例：一个人开着布加迪 Chiron 在 Autobahn 上飙到每小时400公里，还拍下来传到 YouTube 上。结果有人起诉他，理由是尽管没有限速，但法律禁止“鲁莽驾驶”。最后他赢了官司——因为他并没有鲁莽驾驶，只是开得非常非常快而已。

(05:02:32) I’ve done the Autobahn a couple of times. My wife and I went on a road trip in Europe in 2009, and I got the Lamborghini Gallardo we were driving up to 200 miles an hour. And I’d driven 200 miles an hour or close to it on a racetrack before. That feels like one thing. Driving on a public road 200 miles an hour feels really, really fast.
（05:02:32）我上过几次 Autobahn。2009年我和妻子在欧洲自驾游，当时开的兰博基尼 Gallardo 跑到了每小时200英里。以前我也在赛道上开过接近或达到200英里的速度，但那是一种感觉；而在公共道路上以200英里时速行驶，那才叫真正、真正地快。

Lex Fridman
(05:02:52) Scary?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（05:02:52）吓人吗？

DHH
(05:02:54) Actually a little scary, yes, because you constantly think, on a racetrack you know the road, you know the surface. You can walk the track in most of the time. You can know if there’s a dip. On a public road you can’t know if there’s suddenly a pothole. Presumably there’s not going to be a pothole on the German Autobahn, but it does feel a little scary, but also exhilarating.
DHH
（05:02:54）确实有点吓人。因为在赛道上，你熟悉路况和路面状况，很多时候甚至可以步行勘察整条赛道，知道哪里有凹陷。但在公共道路上，你永远不知道会不会突然冒出一个坑洞。当然，德国 Autobahn 应该不会有坑，但那种未知感还是会让人有点紧张，同时也非常刺激。

(05:03:13) Speed is just intrinsically, really fun. I don’t know anyone I’ve taken out in a fast car … Well, actually I do know a few people. Most people I take out in a fast car, they grin. It’s a human reaction to grin when you go really fast.
（05:03:13）速度本身就极具乐趣。我几乎没遇到过坐我快车不笑的人……好吧，其实也有几个例外。但大多数人坐上快车都会咧嘴笑——这是人类面对极速时的自然反应。

Lex Fridman
(05:03:28) Do you know what’s the fastest you’ve ever gone?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（05:03:28）你知道你有史以来最快跑过多快吗？

DHH
(05:03:31) It was probably at Le Mans, I think when the LMP2s were at their maximum power and had 600 horsepower and really sticky tires, we were going 340 kilometers an hour, which is just over 200 miles an hour, a bit over 200 miles an hour. That does feel fast.
DHH
（05:03:31）可能是在勒芒赛道吧。我记得当时 LMP2 赛车处于最大功率状态，有600马力，配上抓地力极强的轮胎，我们跑到了每小时340公里，也就是略高于200英里。那确实感觉飞快。

(05:03:47) And it’s really interesting with speed, is that the difference between going, let’s say 150 and 160 doesn’t feel that much actually, those 10 miles an hour. But the difference between going 190 and 200 feels crazy faster, which as a percentage change is actually less than going from 150 to 160, but there’s some sense of exponentiality once you get up to those limits, where it’s just on a completely different level.
（05:03:47）速度这件事很有意思：比如从150英里加速到160英里，这10英里的差距其实感觉不大；但从190英里到200英里，却感觉快得离谱——尽管从百分比来看，后者的增幅其实比前者还小。但一旦接近极限，速度带来的感受似乎呈指数级增长，完全是另一个维度的体验。

Lex Fridman
(05:04:16) Yeah, because to me, 110, 120 feels fast. 200, that’s crazy.
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（05:04:16）是啊，对我来说，110、120就已经很快了。200？那简直疯狂。

DHH
(05:04:24) It really is crazy.
DHH
（05:04:24）真的非常疯狂。

Programming setup

编程环境

Lex Fridman
(05:04:26) I got to ask you about the details of your programming setup, the IDE, all that kind of stuff. Let’s paint the picture of the perfect programming setup. Do you have a programming setup that you enjoy? Are you very flexible? How many monitors? What kind of keyboard? What kind of chair? What kind of desk?
莱克斯·弗里德曼
（05:04:26）我得问问你关于你的编程环境细节——IDE、各种工具之类的。让我们描绘一下“理想编程环境”的画面。你有没有一套自己特别喜欢的配置？你对设备要求灵活吗？用几块显示器？什么键盘？什么椅子？什么桌子？

DHH
(05:04:51) It’s funny because if you’d asked me, let’s see, a year and a half ago, I would’ve given you the same answer as I would’ve given anyone for basically 20 years. I want a Mac. I like the Magic Keyboard. I like the single monitor. Apple makes an awesome 6K 32-inch XDR screen that I still haven’t found anyone who’ve beaten that I still use. Even though I switched away from Apple computers, I still use their monitor because it’s just fantastic. But I’ve always been a single screen kind of guy.
DHH
（05:04:51）有趣的是，如果你一年半前问我这个问题，我会给出和过去20年几乎完全相同的答案：我要一台 Mac，我喜欢妙控键盘，也只用一块显示器。苹果有一款超棒的32英寸6K XDR 显示器，至今我还没发现有谁能超越它，所以我还在用。即使我已经不再使用苹果电脑，仍然保留着这台显示器，因为它实在太出色了。我一直都是单屏用户。

(05:05:25) I do like a big screen, but I don’t want multiple screens. I’ve never found that, that really works with my perception. I want to be able to just focus on a single thing. I don’t want all of it all over the place, and I’ve always used multiple virtual desktops and being able to switch back and forth between those things.

(05:14:58) 很多人认为这是个大问题，他们会说：“哦，它需要更多功能，需要这些东西。”而我却觉得，自从 Allan 十多年前停止开发后，这款文本编辑器基本没变过，但我对此完全满意，不需要别的。正如我们之前讨论的那样，我不想要一个集成开发环境（IDE），不想让编辑器替我写代码；我只想要一个文本编辑器，让我能直接和字符打交道。

(05:15:25) And Neovim allows me to do that in some ways that are even better than TextMate, and I love TextMate. (05:15:25) 而 Neovim 在某些方面甚至比 TextMate 更能满足我的需求，尽管我真的很喜欢 TextMate。你也知道，Vi 一旦你掌握了命令——听起来可能有点……我有时觉得 Vi 的粉丝们夸大了它的学习难度，仿佛这样能显得他们更厉害似的。其实没那么难。依我看，花不了太久时间，你就能学会足够多的组合操作，然后突然意识到：“天啊，这在其他任何编辑器里都做不到。”

(05:16:08) 你以后会有惊喜的。大概……我是在一年前切换的，头三天一直在骂娘，觉得这玩意儿糟透了，根本不可能用得起来，整整三天都很烦躁。但到了下一周，我就觉得：“这太棒了，我哪儿也不去了。”

(05:16:26) But I also had a bit of a headstart. About 20 years ago in the early 2000s, I tried Vim for a summer and it didn’t stick. I didn’t, for whatever reason, love it at the time. But Neovim is really good.
(05:16:26) 不过我也有一点先发优势。大约二十年前，也就是 2000 年代初，我曾在一个夏天尝试过 Vim，但没坚持下来。当时不知为何就是不喜欢。但 Neovim 真的很好。

(05:16:40) The key to Neovim is to realize that you don’t have to build the whole damn editor yourself. So a lot of Neovim stans are like, “Here’s how to write the config from scratch.” Over 17 episodes, that’s going to take you three weeks. I don’t care that much.
(05:16:40) 使用 Neovim 的关键在于意识到：你不必从头开始自己构建整个编辑器。很多 Neovim 的狂热粉丝会说：“这是从零开始写配置的方法。”照着做可能要花三周时间看 17 集教程。我才不在乎那么多。

(05:16:54) I love a great editor, I love to tailor it a little bit, but not that much. So you have to pair Neovim with this thing called LazyVim. LazyVim.org is a distribution for Neovim that takes all the drudgery out of getting an amazing editor experience right out of the box.
(05:16:54) 我喜欢优秀的编辑器，也喜欢稍微定制一下，但不想折腾太多。所以你应该搭配一个叫 LazyVim 的东西。LazyVim.org 是一个 Neovim 发行版，能让你开箱即用地获得出色的编辑体验，省去所有繁琐配置。

Lex Fridman
(05:17:14) Ridiculous question. We talked about a bunch of programming languages. You told us how much you love JavaScript. It’s your second favorite programming language. Would TypeScript be the third then?
(05:17:14) 问个荒谬的问题。我们聊了很多编程语言。你说过你有多爱 JavaScript，它是你第二喜欢的编程语言。那 TypeScript 会是第三吗？

DHH
(05:17:26) TypeScript wouldn’t even be in this universe. I hate TypeScript as much as I like JavaScript.
(05:17:26) TypeScript 根本不在这个宇宙里。我对 TypeScript 的厌恶程度，跟我对 JavaScript 的喜爱程度一样深。

Lex Fridman
(05:17:33) You hate… Oh, man. I’m not smart enough to understand the math of that. Okay. Before I ask about other programming languages, if you can encapsulate your hatred of TypeScript into something that could be human-interpretable, what would be the reasoning?
(05:17:33) 你讨厌……天哪，我脑子不够用，算不出这个等式。好吧，在我问其他编程语言之前，如果你能把对 TypeScript 的厌恶总结成普通人能理解的理由，那会是什么？

DHH
(05:17:50) JavaScript smells a lot like Ruby when it comes to some aspects of its metaprogramming, and TypeScript just complicates that to an infuriating degree when you’re trying to write that kind of code. And even when you’re trying to write the normal kind of code, none of the benefits that accrue to people who like it, like auto-completion, is something I care about. I don’t care about auto-completion because I’m not using an IDE.
(05:17:50) 在元编程的某些方面，JavaScript 闻起来很像 Ruby，而 TypeScript 在你写这类代码时，却把它复杂化到令人抓狂的程度。即使你只是写普通代码，那些 TypeScript 爱好者所看重的好处——比如自动补全——我也不在乎。我不需要自动补全，因为我根本不用 IDE。

(05:18:14) Now, I understand that that is part of what separates it and why I don’t see the benefits. I only see the costs. I see the extra typing, I see the type gymnastics that you sometimes have to do and where a bunch of people give up and just do any instead, right? That they don’t actually use the type system because it’s just too frustrating to use.
(05:18:14) 我明白，这正是分歧所在，也是为什么我看不见它的优点。我只看到代价：额外的类型标注、有时不得不做的类型杂技，以及很多人最后干脆放弃，直接用 any——因为他们根本没法愉快地使用这套类型系统。

(05:18:35) So I’ve ever only felt the frustration of TypeScript and the obfuscation of TypeScript in the code that gave me no payoff. Again, I understand that there is a payoff. I don’t want the payoff. So for my situation, I’m not willing to make the trade and I’m not willing to take a language that underneath is as dynamic of a language as Ruby is and then turn it into this pretend statically typed language. I find that just intellectually insulting.
(05:18:35) 所以我感受到的只有 TypeScript 带来的挫败感和代码中的晦涩，而这些对我毫无回报。再次强调，我理解它确实有回报，只是我不想要。就我个人而言，我不愿做这种交换——不愿把一种底层本质上和 Ruby 一样动态的语言，硬生生变成一种假装静态类型的语言。我觉得这在智力上是一种侮辱。

Lex Fridman
(05:19:08) Do you think it will and do you think it should die, TypeScript?
(05:19:08) 你觉得 TypeScript 会消亡吗？你觉得它应该消亡吗？

DHH
(05:19:12) I don’t want to take something away from people who enjoy it. So if you like TypeScript, all the power to you. If you’re using TypeScript because you think that’s what a professional program is supposed to do, here’s my permission; you don’t have to use TypeScript.
(05:19:12) 我不想剥夺喜欢它的人的乐趣。所以如果你喜欢 TypeScript，那祝你好运。但如果你用 TypeScript 只是因为你觉得“专业程序员就该这么干”，那我给你许可：你其实没必要用 TypeScript。

Lex Fridman
(05:19:24) There’s something deeply enjoyable about a brilliant programmer such as yourself, DHH, talking shit. It’s one of my favorite things in life. What are the top three programming languages everyone should learn if you’re talking to a beginner?
(05:19:24) 像你这样才华横溢的程序员（DHH）吐槽别人，真的特别让人愉快。这是我人生中最喜欢的事情之一。如果你要给初学者推荐，哪三种编程语言是每个人都该学的？

Programming language for beginners

初学者的编程语言

DHH
(05:19:41) I would 100% start with Ruby. It is magic for beginners in terms of just understanding the core concepts of conditionals and loops and whatever, because it makes it so easy. Even if you’re just making a shell program that’s outputting to the terminal, getting hello-world running in Ruby is basically puts, P-U-T-S, space, start quotes, “Hello world,” end quotes, you’re done, right? There’s no fluff, there’s nothing to wrap it into.
(05:19:41) 我百分之百推荐从 Ruby 开始。对于初学者理解条件语句、循环等核心概念来说，Ruby 就像魔法一样简单。哪怕你只是写一个向终端输出内容的命令行程序，“Hello World” 在 Ruby 中基本上就是输入 puts（P-U-T-S），加个空格，打上引号，“Hello world”，再闭合引号，就完成了！没有多余的东西，也不需要任何包装。

(05:20:10) There are other languages that does that, especially the Perl or Python would be rather similar, but Go would not, Java would not. There’s a lot of other languages that have a lot more ceremony and boilerplate. Ruby has none of it. So it’s a wonderful starting language.
(05:20:10) 其他语言也有类似特性，尤其是 Perl 或 Python 相当接近，但 Go 不行，Java 更不行。很多其他语言都有大量仪式性和样板代码，而 Ruby 完全没有。所以它是一门极佳的入门语言。

(05:20:26) There’s a book called Learn to Program by Pine that uses Ruby essentially to just teach basic programming principles that I’ve seen heavily recommended. So that’s a great language.
(05:20:26) 有一本叫《Learn to Program》的书，作者是 Pine，基本上就是用 Ruby 来教授基础编程原理，我见过很多人强烈推荐。所以 Ruby 真的很棒。

Lex Fridman
(05:20:38) How quickly would you go to Rails?
(05:20:38) 你会多快转向 Rails？

DHH
(05:20:39) It depends on what you want to do. If you want to build web applications, go to Rails right away, learn Ruby along with Rails. Because I think what really helps power through learning programming is to build programs that you want. Right? If you’re just learning it in the abstract, it’s difficult to motivate yourself to actually do it well.
(05:20:39) 这取决于你想做什么。如果你想构建 Web 应用，那就立刻上手 Rails，边学 Ruby 边学 Rails。因为我觉得，真正推动你学好编程的，是去构建你自己想要的程序。对吧？如果你只是抽象地学习，很难激励自己真正把它学好。

(05:20:56) Some people learn languages just for the fun of them. Most people do not. Most people learn it because they have a mission; they want to build a program, they want to become a programmer. So you got to use it for something real. And I actually find that it’s easier to learn programming that way too because it drives your learning process.
(05:20:56) 有些人学编程纯粹是为了乐趣，但大多数人不是这样。大多数人是因为有目标——想做一个程序，想成为程序员。所以你必须用它去做点实实在在的东西。而且我发现，这样学编程反而更容易，因为它能驱动你的学习过程。

(05:21:12) You can’t just learn the whole thing upfront. You can’t just sit down and read the language specification and then go like, “Ooh,” like Neo, “Now I know kung fu. Now I know Ruby.” It doesn’t download that way. You actually have to type it out in anger on a real program.
(05:21:12) 你不可能一开始就掌握全部内容。你不能坐下来读完语言规范，然后像尼奥那样说：“噢，我现在会功夫了，我会 Ruby 了。” 编程不是这样下载到脑子里的。你必须在真实的项目中一边敲代码一边摸索，甚至带着点怒气去写。

Lex Fridman
(05:21:29) Yeah. Yeah, for sure.
(05:21:29) 是啊，确实如此。
DHH
(05:21:30) So I would start there. But then number two probably would be JavaScript because JavaScript just is the language you need to know if you want to work with the web, and the web is the greatest application platform of all time if you’re making business software or collaboration software, all this kind of stuff.
(05:21:47) If you’re making video games, you should probably go off and learn C++ or C or something else like that. But if you’re in the realm of web applications, you got to learn JavaScript. Regardless of what else you learn, you got to learn JavaScript.

DHH
（05:21:30）我会从那里开始。但第二门语言很可能就是 JavaScript，因为如果你想从事 Web 开发，JavaScript 就是你必须掌握的语言；而 Web 是有史以来最伟大的应用平台——尤其是当你在开发商业软件、协作软件等这类东西时。
（05:21:47）如果你要做视频游戏，那你可能应该去学 C++、C 或其他类似的语言。但如果你身处 Web 应用领域，你就必须学习 JavaScript。无论你还学什么别的语言，JavaScript 都是必学的。

Lex Fridman
(05:21:58) So if you’re learning Ruby, what does Ruby not have in terms of programming concepts that you would need other languages for?

Lex Fridman
（05:21:58）那么，如果你在学习 Ruby，它在编程概念方面有哪些缺失，以至于你需要借助其他语言来弥补？

DHH
(05:22:09) I don’t know if there’s any concepts missing, but it doesn’t have the speed or the low-level access of memory manipulation-
Lex Fridman
(05:22:17) Sure.
DHH
(05:22:17) … that you would need to build a 3D gaming engine, for example. No one’s going to build that in Ruby. You could build quite low-level stuff when it comes to web technologies in Ruby, but at some point, you’re going to hit the limit and you should use something else.
(05:22:32) I’m not someone who prescribes just Ruby for everything. Just once you reach the level of abstraction that’s involved with web applications, Ruby is superb. But if you’re writing, for example, a HTTP proxy, Go is great for that. We’ve written quite a few HTTP proxies lately at the company for various reasons, including our cloud exit and so forth.
(05:22:54) And Kevin, one of the programmers I’m working with, he writes all of that in Go. Go just have the primitives and it has the pace and the speed to do that really well. I highly recommend it. If you’re writing an HTTP general proxy, do it in Go. Great language for that. Don’t write your business logic in Go. I know people do, but I don’t see the point in that.

DHH
（05:22:09）我不确定 Ruby 是否真的缺少某些编程概念，但它确实缺乏速度和底层内存操作的能力——
Lex Fridman
（05:22:17）当然。
DHH
（05:22:17）——比如你若要构建一个 3D 游戏引擎，Ruby 就不合适。没人会用 Ruby 去做那种事。在 Web 技术领域，Ruby 其实也能实现相当底层的功能，但到某个程度后，你会碰到性能瓶颈，那时就该换用别的语言了。
（05:22:32）我并不是那种主张“什么都用 Ruby”的人。但一旦你进入 Web 应用所涉及的抽象层级，Ruby 的表现就非常出色。不过，举个例子，如果你要写一个 HTTP 代理，Go 就特别适合。我们公司最近出于各种原因（包括云迁移退出等）写了不少 HTTP 代理。
（05:22:54）我和一位叫 Kevin 的程序员合作，他全用 Go 来写这些代理。Go 拥有合适的底层原语，也有足够的性能和速度来高效完成这类任务。我强烈推荐它。如果你要写通用的 HTTP 代理，就用 Go——它在这方面非常棒。但别用 Go 写业务逻辑。我知道有人这么做，但我看不出这样做的意义。

Lex Fridman

DHH
(05:23:19) Yeah. If you’re interested in working with the web, I’d probably pick those three. Go, Ruby, and JavaScript.

DHH
（05:23:19）是的。如果你对 Web 开发感兴趣，我大概会选这三门：Go、Ruby 和 JavaScript。

DHH
(05:23:41) I love that there are people who love functional languages to that degree. Those people are not me. I don’t care at all. I care about functional principles when they help me in these isolated cases where that’s just better than everything else. But at heart, I’m an object-oriented guy. That’s just how I think about programs. That’s how I like to think about programs. That’s how I carve up a big problem space into the main language. Objects are my jam.

DHH
（05:23:41）我很欣赏那些对函数式语言如此热爱的人。但那些人不是我。我完全不在意。只有当函数式原则在某些特定场景下明显优于其他方法时，我才关心它们。但本质上，我是个面向对象的人。这就是我思考程序的方式，也是我喜欢思考程序的方式，更是我将大型问题空间分解为主语言结构的方式。对象才是我的菜。

Lex Fridman
(05:24:10) Yeah, me too. So I program in Lisp a bunch for AI applications for basic… So, Othello, chess engines, that kind of stuff. And I did try OCaml just to force myself to program just a very basic Game of Life, a little simulation. Lisp is just parentheses everywhere. It’s actually not readable at all.

Lex Fridman
（05:24:10）是啊，我也是。我经常用 Lisp 编写一些基础的 AI 应用程序，比如黑白棋（Othello）、国际象棋引擎之类的东西。我也试过 OCaml，强迫自己用它写了一个非常基础的“生命游戏”小模拟。Lisp 到处都是括号，其实根本读不下去。

DHH

DHH

Lex Fridman
(05:24:50) Yeah. But I have to figure out, I’m sure there’s an answer to this, what can I do that would be useful for me that I actually want to build?

DHH
(05:24:58) Yes. That’s my problem.
